## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear oscillator with periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 - x**2) (nonlinear damping depending on position)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum with drive: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (combined nonlinearities)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect odd polynomial in x for symmetric potentials
- Even-power terms in x (x²) indicate asymmetric potential wells and should appear when oscillation is not symmetric
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v*(1 - x²) indicate amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol type self-excitation)
- Sinusoidal dependence on x (sin(cx)) suggests a periodic potential like a pendulum rather than polynomial restoring force
- Explicit time dependence through cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicates external periodic driving force
- Products of x and v (e.g., x*v, x²*v) indicate coupling between restoring and dissipative mechanisms
- Parametric excitation appears as x*cos(c*t) where stiffness is modulated periodically in time
- If acceleration has no explicit time dependence, the system is autonomous and phase-plane analysis applies — try formulas only in x and v

- `-0.0441723*v**3`
- `-0.333481*v + 0.333481*v**3`
- `-1.24947*v`
- `-3.58221*x*0.047928*|v|^(1/3) - 3.58221*x`
- `-0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

- **v³**: `-0.0441723 + 0.333481 = 0.289309` → `0.289309*v**3`
- **v**: `-0.333481 - 1.24947 = -1.58295` → `-1.58295*v`
- **x**: `-3.58221*x`
- **x*|v|^(1/3)**: `-3.58221*0.047928*x*|v|^(1/3) ≈ -0.17166*x*|v|^(1/3)`
- **log(|v|+1)**: `-0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

So GT = `A*x + B*v + C*v**3 + D*x*|v|^(1/3) + E*log(|v| + 1)`
